## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: materials science & solid mechanics (thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling)
**Analysis**: The variables are stress (sigma), strain (epsilon), and temperature (T), which most directly indicates a constitutive law for a solid under thermo-mechanical loading. Common relationships include elastic/plastic stress–strain curves with temperature-dependent modulus and temperature-driven softening of yield/flow stress.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear elasticity (Hooke): sigma = c0 * epsilon (small-strain, isothermal elastic regime)
- Temperature-dependent modulus: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (elastic stiffness changes approximately linearly with temperature)
- Inverse temperature modulus (softening): sigma = (c0 + c1 / (T + c2)) * epsilon (elastic modulus decreases with increasing T over a range)
- Thermoelastic with thermal strain offset: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * (T - c2)) (stress from mechanical strain minus thermal expansion strain)
- Nonlinear elastic polynomial: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (moderate-strain elastic nonlinearity)
- Symmetric nonlinear elasticity: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon * Abs(epsilon) (odd-in-epsilon stress with stiffening/softening)
- Power-law (Hollomon-type) hardening: sigma = c0 * (Abs(epsilon) + c1)**c2 * Sign(epsilon) (plastic flow curve / hardening in monotonic loading)
- Temperature-softened power-law flow: sigma = (c0 * (Abs(epsilon) + c1)**c2) * exp(c3 * T) * Sign(epsilon) (flow stress decreases/increases exponentially with T depending on sign of c3)
- Ramberg–Osgood implicit form (often rearranged for sigma): epsilon = c0 * sigma + c1 * sigma**c2 (combined elastic + plastic strain; invertible in fitting)
- Johnson–Cook-like (without strain-rate term): sigma = (c0 + c1 * (Abs(epsilon) + c2)**c3) * (c4 + c5 * (T - c6)) (work hardening multiplied by a temperature softening factor)
- Sigmoid transition (yield/phase-like change with T): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon) * (c2 + c3 * tanh(c4 * (T - c5))) (smooth transition in stiffness/strength near a characteristic temperature)
- Coupled quadratic interaction: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * T + c2 * epsilon * T (first-order thermo-mechanical coupling in a regression-friendly form)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Elastic regime identification: near epsilon ≈ 0, sigma is typically odd in epsilon and approximately linear (suggests sigma ≈ E(T)*epsilon).
- Thermal expansion offset: if stress vanishes at nonzero epsilon that shifts with T, include an additive thermal-strain term epsilon - c*(T-c0).
- Temperature softening of stiffness/strength: decreasing slope d(sigma)/d(epsilon) with increasing T suggests E(T) that decreases with T (often linear, reciprocal, or exponential forms).
- Work hardening signature: if d(sigma)/d(epsilon) decreases with epsilon while sigma increases, power-law or saturating hardening structures are likely.
- Tension–compression symmetry: if sigma(epsilon) ≈ -sigma(-epsilon), use odd forms like epsilon, epsilon*Abs(epsilon), or apply Sign(epsilon) with Abs(epsilon) in magnitude terms.
- Transition temperature behavior: abrupt changes in stress level with T (e.g., near glass transition) often fit better with tanh/logistic-like temperature factors than with simple polynomials.
- Cross-term necessity: if the shape of the stress–strain curve changes with T (not just scaled up/down), include interaction terms like epsilon*T or temperature-dependent exponents/coefficient factors.
- Nonphysical divergence control: if models blow up at high T or large epsilon, prefer bounded temperature multipliers (e.g., tanh-based) or shifted denominators (T+c) rather than high-degree polynomials.

## Candidate-by-candidate analysis

### Candidates 1–8 (no \(T\) dependence at all)
1–8 are functions of \(\epsilon\) only (sines/rationals/exp/polynomials). GT depends on both \(\epsilon\) **and** \(T\) (nontrivially). No domain restriction can remove \(T\) from GT for all points in a continuous domain (unless you restrict to \(T=T_0\) exactly, which is not a “plausible continuous domain condition” in the sense of an interval/half-line).  
**⇒ 1–8 cannot match.**

### Candidates 9–15 (have \(T\) but only through rational forms like \(T*\frac{\epsilon^2}{c1+\epsilon}\) or \(T*c2\))
These candidates have \(T\) appearing as:
- \(T\cdot \frac{\epsilon^2}{c1+\epsilon}\), \(T\cdot \frac{\epsilon}{c1+\epsilon}\), or \(T\cdot c2\),
and the rest are rational-in-\(\epsilon\) and/or oscillatory \(\sin(\log(\cdot))\) divided by \((c1+\epsilon)\).

GT’s \(T\)-dependence is **polynomial-like in \(\epsilon\)**: coefficient of \(T\) is a sum of \(\epsilon\) and \(\epsilon^{0.5976}\) terms (plus constant). None of 9–15 can produce an \(\epsilon^{0.5976}\) factor multiplying \(T\) because:
- they only have integer powers of \(\epsilon\) in numerators (\(\epsilon,\epsilon^2\)) and a linear denominator \((c1+\epsilon)\), yielding rational functions, not fractional powers;
- the \(\sin(\log(\cdot))\) terms cannot equal a pure power \(\epsilon^{0.5976}\) on any open interval (analytic/oscillatory mismatch), unless their coefficients are set to 0, in which case no fractional power remains.

Also, GT has a clean \((T-T_0)\) shift; candidates have no way to enforce the same shift except by expanding constants, but they still cannot generate the fractional power term.  
**⇒ 9–15 cannot match.**

### Candidates 16, 18, 19 (linear in \(T\) and \(\epsilon\), plus rational/sin/abs)
16: \(T*c0 + T*c1*\epsilon + c2/(c3+\epsilon) + c4\sin(\log(\cdot)) + c8\).  
18: similar but with \(c8|\epsilon|\).  
19: similar but with \(c8\epsilon\).

GT needs \(T\)-coefficient containing \(\epsilon^{0.5976}\). These candidates only allow \(T\) times (constant + \(\epsilon\)). No fractional power in \(T\)-coefficient is possible. Setting the rational and sine parts to 0 can remove them, but still no \(\epsilon^{0.5976}(T-T_0)\) term. Domain restrictions like \(\epsilon\ge 0\) can turn \(|\epsilon|\) into \(\epsilon\), but still not \(\epsilon^{0.5976}\).  
**⇒ 16, 18, 19 cannot match.**

### Candidate 17, 21, 42 (no \(T\); variants of 1–7)
No \(T\) dependence.  
**⇒ cannot match.**

### Candidate 20, 22–24 (rational \(T*\epsilon^2/(c1+\epsilon)\) etc.)
Same core issue as 9–15: \(T\) enters via rational functions and/or lacks any fractional power \(\epsilon^{0.5976}\) multiplying \(T\). Candidate 22 also has stray additive \(c1\) and \(+\epsilon\) etc., but none can create \(\epsilon^{0.5976}(T-T_0)\).  
**⇒ 20, 22–24 cannot match.**

### Candidate 25 (polynomial in \(\epsilon\) plus \(T*c0*\epsilon\), plus \(1/(c8+\epsilon)\))
Has \(T*c0*\epsilon\) but no \(\epsilon^{0.5976}T\) term; also includes \(1/(c8+\epsilon)\) which GT does not have (must be killed by setting coefficient to 0, but it’s fixed as 1 here, so cannot).  
**⇒ cannot match.**

### Candidates 26–28 (contain logs/sin and rational terms; \(T*c0*\epsilon\) at best)
26: includes \(\epsilon/(c8\epsilon+c9)\) and \(1/(c8\epsilon+c9)\) which cannot be removed simultaneously unless you do something singular; GT has no such rational singularities. Also no \(\epsilon^{0.5976}T\).  
27: still has \(1/(c8\epsilon+c9)\) fixed; cannot match GT.  
28: \(T*c0*\epsilon + \sin(\log(\cdot)) + 1/(c5+\epsilon)\) with fixed rational term; cannot match.

**⇒ 26–28 cannot match.**

### Candidates 29–30 (linear in \(T\) and \(\epsilon\), plus sine(log) and \(1/(c7+\epsilon)\))
Both have a fixed \(1/(c7+\epsilon)\) term (coefficient 1), which GT lacks; cannot be eliminated. Also no fractional power term.  
**⇒ cannot match.**

### Candidate 31 (Max, abs, plus fixed \(1/(c9+\epsilon)\))
Contains non-smooth Max and a fixed rational \(1/(c9+\epsilon)\) term; GT has neither. Cannot eliminate fixed rational.  
**⇒ cannot match.**

### Candidate 32 (linear \(T*c0*\epsilon\) + sine(log) + \(1/(c7+\epsilon)\))
Again fixed \(1/(c7+\epsilon)\) term cannot be removed.  
**⇒ cannot match.**

### Candidate 33 (has \(c6*exp(T*c7)*log(\cdot)\) and fixed \(1/(c9+\epsilon)\))
Fixed rational term + exponential-in-\(T\) (GT is affine in \(T\)). Even if \(c6=0\) to remove exp, fixed rational remains.  
**⇒ cannot match.**

### Candidate 34–35 (contain fixed \(1/(c8+\epsilon)\) or \(1/(c5+\epsilon)\))
Both have unavoidable rational term with coefficient 1; GT has none.  
**⇒ cannot match.**

### Candidate 36 (has \(\epsilon\sin(T*c7+c8)\) and fixed \(1/(c9+\epsilon)\))
Fixed rational term cannot be removed; also sinusoidal in \(T\) unless coefficient set 0, but still fixed rational remains.  
**⇒ cannot match.**

### Candidate 37 (has \(\sin(\log(T*c4 + c5|\epsilon|+1))\), exp in \(\epsilon\), and fixed \(1/(c9+\epsilon)\))
Fixed rational term; also non-affine in \(T\).  
**⇒ cannot match.**

### Candidate 38 (has \(\epsilon|\epsilon|\) and fixed \(1/(c7+\epsilon)\))
Fixed rational term cannot be removed.  
**⇒ cannot match.**

### Candidate 39 (has \(T^{c1}c2\) and fixed \(1/(c8+\epsilon)\))
Non-affine in \(T\) unless special exponents, but still fixed rational term cannot be removed.  
**⇒ cannot match.**

### Candidate 40 (has \(T*c0*\epsilon\) + \(c2/(c3+\epsilon)\) + sine(log) + \(\epsilon|\epsilon|\))
No fixed rational coefficient 1 here, but still:
- cannot generate \(\epsilon^{0.5976}(T-T_0)\) because \(T\) only multiplies \(\epsilon\) (no fractional power),
- extra rational/sine terms must be set to 0 (possible), but fractional power term still missing.  
**⇒ cannot match.**

### Candidate 41 (has fixed \(1/(c6+\epsilon)\))
Fixed rational term cannot be removed.  
**⇒ cannot match.**

### Candidate 43 (linear in \(T\) and \(\epsilon\), plus \(\epsilon|\epsilon|\) and fixed \(1/(c7+\epsilon)\))
Fixed rational term cannot be removed.  
**⇒ cannot match.**

### Candidate 44 (rational \(T*\epsilon^2/(c1+\epsilon)\) etc., with fixed \(1/(c1+\epsilon)\) terms)
Even aside from missing fractional power, it has multiple unavoidable \(1/(c1+\epsilon)\) contributions (some coefficients are fixed as 1). GT has none.  
**⇒ cannot match.**

### Candidate 45 (has \(T*c0*\epsilon\) + exp(\(\epsilon\)) + fixed \(1/(c8+\epsilon)\))
Fixed rational term cannot be removed.  
**⇒ cannot match.**

### Candidate 46–47 (affine-ish in \(T\) but include fixed \(1/(c8+\epsilon)\) or \(1/(c9+\epsilon)\))
Both have unavoidable rational term with coefficient 1; GT has none.  
**⇒ cannot match.**

### Candidate 48 (has sine(log(T*c4 + c5|ε|+1)) and fixed \(1/(c7+\epsilon)\))
Fixed rational term cannot be removed.  
**⇒ cannot match.**

### Candidate 49–50 (rational \(T*\epsilon^2/(c1+\epsilon)\) etc., plus fixed \(1/(c1+\epsilon)\))
Contain unavoidable \(1/(c1+\epsilon)\) term with coefficient 1; GT has none. Also cannot create \(\epsilon^{0.5976}T\).  
**⇒ cannot match.**

---

### Overall conclusion
No candidate has the essential GT structure: an affine function of \(T\) whose \(T\)-coefficient includes a genuine fractional power \(\epsilon^{0.597577...}\), and many candidates also contain unavoidable rational terms \(1/(c+\epsilon)\) with fixed coefficient 1 that GT does not have.

[NO MATCH]

Conclusion: No match

GT: c0*epsilon*(-c1*(T - c2) + c3) - c4*(T - c5) + epsilon**c6*c7*(T - c8)
Candidates evaluated: 50

I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) and compare each candidate to it.

## Ground Truth Analysis

The GT expression is:
```
31.12*epsilon*(-0.05295*(T - 316.19) + 1) - 0.2255*(T - 316.19) + epsilon^0.5976 * 3.629*(T - 316.19)
```

Let me expand this:
- Term 1: `31.12*epsilon*(-0.05295*T + 0.05295*316.19 + 1)` = `31.12*epsilon*(-0.05295*T + 17.74)` = `-1.648*epsilon*T + 551.8*epsilon`
- Term 2: `-0.2255*T + 71.31`
- Term 3: `3.629*epsilon^0.5976*T - 3.629*316.19*epsilon^0.5976` = `3.629*epsilon^0.5976*T - 1147.5*epsilon^0.5976`

So GT = `-1.648*epsilon*T + 551.8*epsilon - 0.2255*T + 71.31 + 3.629*epsilon^0.5976*T - 1147.5*epsilon^0.5976`

The key basis functions in GT are:
1. `epsilon*T` (linear in both)
2. `epsilon` (linear)
3. `T` (linear)
4. Constant
5. `epsilon^0.5976 * T` (fractional power times T)
6. `epsilon^0.5976` (fractional power)

The critical feature is `epsilon^0.5976` - a fractional power of epsilon, and its product with T.

## Candidate Analysis

Now I need to check which candidates can produce these basis functions. The key distinguishing feature is `epsilon^0.5976` (approximately `epsilon^0.6`), which is NOT equivalent to any standard function like sin, exp, log, polynomial, or rational function.

**Candidates 1-8, 17, 21, 42**: These use `sin`, `exp`, rational functions, and polynomials in epsilon only (no T dependence in the structure). They lack T as a variable entirely, so they cannot match GT which depends on T.

**Candidates 9-15, 20, 22-24, 44, 49-50**: These involve `sin(c*log(c*|epsilon|+1))`. Note that `sin(c*log(c*|epsilon|+1))` is an oscillatory function - it cannot match `epsilon^0.5976` which is monotonic. These cannot match.

**Candidates 16, 18-19, 25, 28-43, 45-48**: These also use `sin(c*log(c*|epsilon|+1))` or `sin(c*epsilon)` combined with T terms. The `sin(log(...))` function oscillates and cannot replicate `epsilon^0.5976 * T`.

Wait - let me reconsider. `sin(c3*log(c4*|epsilon|+1) + c5)` with appropriate constants... if `c4` is very large, `log(c4*epsilon+1) ≈ log(c4*epsilon)` for large epsilon, but this is an approximation, not exact. The function `sin(a*log(x) + b)` oscillates infinitely as x grows, while `epsilon^0.6` is monotonically increasing. These are fundamentally different.

Similarly, `exp(c*epsilon)` grows exponentially while `epsilon^0.6` grows sub-linearly - no match possible.

For candidates with `epsilon*|epsilon|` = `epsilon^2` (for epsilon ≥ 0), this gives polynomial terms, not fractional powers.

None of the candidates contain `epsilon^c` with a free fractional exponent that could match `epsilon^0.5976`.

After careful analysis, **no candidate** can reproduce the fractional power `epsilon^0.5976` that appears in the GT.

Candidate 1-50 verdict: All [NO MATCH]
